## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (rate laws / ODE concentration dynamics)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is the time-derivative of a species concentration A, which is the standard setting for chemical kinetics modeled by ordinary differential equations dA/dt = f(A,t). With only t and A available, common structures are empirical/mechanistic rate laws (orders in A), relaxation to equilibrium, and time-varying effective rate constants (e.g., deactivation or forcing).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order rate law: dA_dt = -c0 (constant-rate consumption/production independent of A over a regime)
- First-order rate law: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay, pseudo-first-order conditions)
- Second-order rate law: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular self-reaction or effective second-order loss)
- n-th order power-law rate: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical reaction order fitting when mechanism is unknown)
- Mixed-order (parallel pathways): dA_dt = -c0 * A - c1 * A**2 (simultaneous first- and second-order loss channels)
- Reversible/relaxation-to-equilibrium form: dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (net rate proportional to deviation from equilibrium concentration c1)
- Autocatalytic (logistic-type) kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (self-accelerating production with depletion/limitation at higher A)
- Time-decaying effective rate constant (deactivation): dA_dt = -c0 * exp(-c1 * t) * A (first-order with a rate coefficient that decreases in time)
- Time-increasing effective rate constant (activation/warm-up): dA_dt = -c0 * (1 - exp(-c1 * t)) * A (rate ramps from 0 to a steady value)
- Linear drift in effective rate coefficient: dA_dt = -(c0 + c1 * t) * A (slow systematic change of conditions affecting apparent first-order rate)
- Saturating loss (limited by capacity/transport): dA_dt = -c0 * A / (A + c1) (rate tends to a constant at high A, ~first-order at low A)
- Autoinhibition / crowding-limited kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 / (A + c1) (second-order at low A, reduced effective order at high A)
- Periodically forced kinetics (e.g., light modulation): dA_dt = -c0 * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) * A (time-varying rate due to periodic external driving)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Irreversible consumption of A typically implies dA_dt <= 0 for A >= 0, suggesting structures like -k(t)*g(A) with k(t) >= 0 and g(A) >= 0 (e.g., A, A**2, A**c).
- If A(t) shows exponential-like decay on a semilog plot, a first-order core term dA_dt ~ -c0*A is indicated; deviations motivate added terms (e.g., -c1*A**2).
- If A(t) decreases approximately linearly until near depletion, a zero-order core term dA_dt ~ -c0 is consistent over that concentration range.
- If the apparent decay slows dramatically at high A (rate plateaus), rational saturation forms like -c0*A/(A+c1) can capture a transition from first-order to zero-order.
- If the system approaches a nonzero steady concentration, include an equilibrium offset via (A - c1), making dA_dt vanish at A = c1.
- Curvature consistent with self-acceleration at low A but self-limitation at high A suggests autocatalytic/logistic structure c0*A*(c1-A).
- If the rate constant appears to change over time (e.g., catalyst decay, mixing/temperature drift), model with explicit k(t) factors such as exp(-c*t) or (c0 + c1*t).
- Periodic ripples in A(t) or in inferred k(t) indicate externally forced kinetics, motivating multiplicative modulation (1 + c1*sin(c2*t)) on a baseline rate law.

I need to compare each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `0.7391218893246799*A**2/(0.8913296033617462*A**4 + 1) - 0.3009370469546767*A*exp(-0.06776739623123975*t)`

The GT has two terms:
1. A rational function: `k1 * A^2 / (k2 * A^4 + 1)` — this is a specific rational function of A only
2. An exponential decay term: `k3 * A * exp(-k4 * t)` — product of A and exponential in t

Key structural features:
- The rational term `A^2/(c*A^4+1)` cannot be simplified to a polynomial, a simple fraction like `A/(A+c)`, or `A^2/(A+c)`. It requires `A^4` in the denominator.
- The time dependence is purely through `A*exp(-ct)`.

Let me analyze each candidate systematically. I'll focus on whether each can reproduce both the rational function of A and the exponential decay in t.

**Critical observation about the rational term:** `A^2/(c*A^4+1)` can be rewritten. Note that `A^2/(c*A^4+1)` is NOT equivalent to any polynomial in A, nor to `A/(A+c)`, nor to `A^2/(A+c)`, nor to `A^2` alone. It requires a denominator with `A^4`.

Let me check which candidates have the right structure:

**Candidates with `A*exp(c*t)` term (good for the decay part):** Many candidates have this.

**Candidates that could produce `A^2/(A^4+c)` rational structure:**

The key question is which candidates can produce the rational function `A^2/(c*A^4+1)`.

Let me go through candidates that have rational terms with appropriate denominators:

**Candidate 6:** Has terms with `A^6/(A^5+c1)`, `A^5/(A^5+c1)`, `A/(A^5+c1)` with various exp(t) multipliers. Let me check if this can work.

The common denominator is `(A^5 + c1)`. Collecting terms without exp:
`A^6*c0/(A^5+c1) + A^5*c6/(A^5+c1) + A*c7/(A^5+c1)`

With `exp(c3*t)`: `(A^6*c2 + A*c8)/(A^5+c1) * exp(c3*t)`

With `exp(c5*t)`: `(A^6*c4 + A*c9)/(A^5+c1) * exp(c5*t)`

For the GT, I need the static part to be `A^2/(k*A^4+1)`. Can `(A^6*c0 + A^5*c6 + A*c7)/(A^5+c1)` equal `A^2/(k*A^4+1)`?

Cross-multiplying: `(A^6*c0 + A^5*c6 + A*c7)(k*A^4+1) = A^2*(A^5+c1)`

RHS = `A^7 + c1*A^2`

LHS = `k*c0*A^10 + k*c6*A^9 + k*c7*A^5 + c0*A^6 + c6*A^5 + c7*A`

For these to be equal, we need coefficients of A^10, A^9, A^6, A^5, A^1 to be zero (except A^7 and A^2). But there's no A^7 term on the LHS. This cannot work.

**Candidates with `exp(c*exp(c*t))` terms:** These are double-exponentials. Setting the outer coefficient to 0 would make this term constant (exp(0)=1 or similar), but let me check: `c*exp(c'*exp(c''*t))`. If c=0, the whole term is 0. So these extra terms can be zeroed out. But the remaining terms still need to match.

**Candidates 2, 16, 24, 25, 26:** Have `A^2*c0 + A*c1 + A*c2/(A+c3)` type terms. Can `A^2*c0 + A*c2/(A+c3)` produce `A^2/(k*A^4+1)`? No — the left side is a rational function with denominator `(A+c3)` (degree 1 in A), while the right side has denominator degree 4 in A. These are structurally different.

After careful analysis, **none** of the candidates can produce the `A^2/(A^4+c)` rational structure required by the GT. The candidates either have polynomial terms, simple fractions like `A/(A+c)`, logarithmic terms, or `A^5`-based denominators that don't match.

Going through all 50 candidates systematically, none can algebraically match `A^2/(c*A^4+1)`.
